## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law relates the reaction rate to the concentration of reactants, potentially with various orders and mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Zero-order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0', 'scenario': 'Reaction rate independent of concentration, e.g., surface-catalyzed reactions at saturation'}
- {'name': 'First-order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A', 'scenario': 'Rate proportional to concentration, radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition'}
- {'name': 'Second-order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2', 'scenario': 'Bimolecular reaction where two molecules of the same species react'}
- {'name': 'General n-th order rate law', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**c1', 'scenario': 'Fractional or arbitrary order kinetics observed in complex reactions'}
- {'name': 'Reversible first-order reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1', 'scenario': 'First-order forward reaction with a constant back-reaction term (equilibrium approach)'}
- {'name': 'Mixed-order kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)', 'scenario': 'Enzyme-like saturation kinetics or Langmuir-Hinshelwood surface reaction'}
- {'name': 'Autocatalytic reaction', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A)', 'scenario': 'Autocatalysis where product catalyzes its own formation, logistic-type rate'}
- {'name': 'Inhibition kinetics', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A**2)', 'scenario': 'Substrate inhibition or product inhibition in catalytic reactions'}
- {'name': 'Consecutive reaction with time dependence', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A * exp(c2 * t)', 'scenario': 'Coupled consecutive reactions where intermediate builds up over time'}
- {'name': 'Power-law with equilibrium offset', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * (A - c1)**c2', 'scenario': 'Reaction approaching equilibrium concentration with general order'}
- {'name': 'Second-order reversible', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2', 'scenario': 'Second-order forward with first-order reverse and constant production'}
- {'name': 'Time-dependent deactivation', 'formula': 'dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Catalyst deactivation or time-varying rate constant'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate with positive concentration → decay kinetics, expect negative coefficient on A terms (consumption)
- Rate approaching zero at specific concentration → equilibrium behavior, look for (A - A_eq) structure
- Rate proportional to A^n with n between 0 and 2 → typical reaction order, try fractional power laws
- Rate independent of time t → autonomous ODE, pure concentration-dependent kinetics (most common in well-mixed reactors)
- Concave-down rate vs concentration curve → saturation or inhibition, use rational functions A/(1+cA) or A/(1+cA^2)
- Rate changes sign at some concentration → reversible reaction with equilibrium, look for linear or polynomial forms with roots
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-isothermal conditions, catalyst aging, or external forcing; use exp(c*t) modulation
- Rate quadratic in A → bimolecular mechanism or autocatalytic pathway, try A*(c0 - A) or c0*A^2 forms

This has three terms:
1. A rational term: `0.826*A²/(0.864*A⁴ + 1)` 
2. A linear term in A: `-0.101*A`
3. An exponential decay term: `-0.101*A*exp(-0.0756*t)`

The key structural features are:
- A²/(A⁴ + const) type rational function
- Linear in A
- A*exp(negative*t) term

Let me check candidates systematically. I'll focus on candidates that could potentially have these three basis functions.

**Candidate 1:** `(A²c0*t + A²c1 + Ac2*t + Ac3 + c4*t + c5)/(c6 + t)`

**Candidate 2:** `A^c0*c1 + c2*exp(c3/A⁵) + c4*exp(c5*sin(A*c6+c7))`

The rational term A²/(0.864A⁴+1) is NOT a polynomial plus c6/A⁵. The Taylor expansion of A²/(0.864A⁴+1) = A² - 0.864A⁶ + ... which has A⁶ terms. A polynomial + 1/A⁵ cannot match this.
